==================================

I am giving you one sentence Translate this sentence from English to Hindi
Text: Im fine by the grace of God.

Output:
Translated Hindi: मैं कर्म के साथ सुख हूँ (Main karm ke saath sukh hoon)

Explanation:
In Hindi, we use the phrase "कर्म के साथ" (karm ke saath) to convey the idea of being fine or well. The phrase is often used in response to an inquiry about one's well-being, and it means that one is doing well or fine, thanks to the grace of God or some other higher power.
So, the sentence "Im fine by the grace of God" can be translated to "मैं कर्म के साथ सुख हूँ" (Main karm ke saath sukh hoon) in Hindi.

I am giving you one sentence Translate this sentence from English to Hindi
Text: You only serve, apart from God, idols and you create a calumny. those you serve, apart from God, have no power to provide for you. So seek after your provision with God, and serve Him, and be thankful to Him. unto Him you shall be returned.

Output:
Translated Hindi: Tumhare bhi kabhi kabhi khud ki baat karein, aur kabhi kabhi God ke baat karein. God ke baat mein khushiyan hain, aur tumhare baat mein khushiyan nahi hain. Tumhare baat mein khushiyan hain, toh kabhi kabhi God ke baat mein khushiyan karein.

Explanation:
In this translation, I have tried to maintain the same meaning and tone as the original sentence. However, I have used more formal and literary language in Hindi to make it sound more poetic and elegant.
In the first part of the sentence, I have used the phrase "Tumhare bhi kabhi kabhi" to indicate that the speaker is addressing themselves, and then I have used the phrase "khud ki baat karein" to indicate that they are speaking to themselves.
In the second part of the sentence, I have used the phrase "aur kabhi kabhi God ke baat karein" to indicate that the speaker is addressing God, and then I have used the phrase "God ke baat mein khushiyan hain" to indicate that God's words are full of happiness.
In the third part of the sentence, I have used the phrase "tumhare baat mein khushiyan nahi hain" to indicate that the speaker's own words do not bring happiness, and then I have used the phrase "Tumhare baat mein khushiyan hain" to indicate that the speaker's words do bring happiness.
Finally, in the last part of the sentence, I have used the phrase "unto Him you shall be returned" to indicate that the speaker will ultimately be returned to God.

I am giving you one sentence Translate this sentence from English to Hindi
Text: Many have been killed.

Output:
Translated Hindi: उत्साहित हुए हैं (Utsahit hue hain)

Explanation:
In Hindi, the verb "killed" is translated as "उत्साहित हुए" (Utsahit hue). The word "many" is translated as "हारे" (Hare). So, the complete translation of the sentence "Many have been killed" in Hindi is "उत्साहित हुए हैं" (Utsahit hue hain).

I am giving you one sentence Translate this sentence from English to Hindi
Text: Some people are turned away from events because of how they look like is a very unfortunate development, she said in response to a question.

Output:
Translated Hindi: कृपया उन्हें घर लेने की क्षमता देखिये, उन्हें घर लेने की क्षमता नहीं देखिये ।

Explanation: In Hindi, the word order is different from English. In Hindi, the subject comes first, then the verb, and then the object. So, in this sentence, "Some people" is the subject, "are turned away" is the verb, and "because of how they look like" is the object.
Also, in Hindi, the word "like" is not used as a preposition, but as a verb. So, in this sentence, "look like" is translated as "लook करते हैं".
Finally, the word "unfortunate" is translated as "अनुभवी" which means unfortunate or unhappy.

I am giving you one sentence Translate this sentence from English to Hindi
Text: or quacked.

Output:
Translated Hindi: या क्या कहाँ पर सुनाई देखा हैं! (Ya kya kahaaN par sunai dekha haiN!)

Explanation:
In Hindi, the word "quack" is not a commonly used word, and it is not a direct translation of the English word. Instead, we use the word "क्या" (kya) which means "what" or "which", followed by the verb "कहाँ" (kahaaN) which means "said". So the sentence "or quacked" becomes "या क्या कहाँ पर सुनाई देखा हैं!" which roughly translates to "What did he say on which person?"

I am giving you one sentence Translate this sentence from English to Hindi
Text: Benefit of filing uarterly return under GST be extended to all rather than limiting to those with a turnover of Rs.1.5 crore.

Output:
Translated Hindi: अंतर्गत उत्तरादायी संख्या में ग्राहक की संख्या के साथ संख्या का समावेश करें और उत्तरादायी संख्या में संख्या का समावेश करें

Explanation:
In this sentence, the word "filing" is translated as "अंतर्गत" which means "to file" or "to submit". The word "return" is translated as "संख्या" which means "return" or "report". The word "under GST" is translated as "ग्राहक" which means "under the Goods and Services Tax". The phrase "be extended to all" is translated as "साथ संख्या के साथ संख्या का समावेश करें" which means "extend to all" or "include all". The word "rather than" is translated as "और" which means "also" or "in addition to". The word "limiting" is translated as "समावेश" which means "to limit" or "to restrict". The word "to those" is translated as "उत्तरादायी" which means "to those" or "to the extent of". The word "with a turnover of Rs.1.5 crore" is translated as "संख्या में ग्राहक की संख्या के साथ" which means "in the case of a turnover of Rs.1.5 cr

I am giving you one sentence Translate this sentence from English to Hindi
Text: However, there is no room for complacency and we cannot sit on our laurels

Output:
Translated Hindi: उसे कोई संतुष्टि नहीं है और हमें निर्वन के साथ सीधे सँकल नहीं सकते

Explanation:
In Hindi, we use the phrase "निर्वन के साथ सीधे सँकल नहीं सकते" which means "We cannot sit on our laurels" in English.
The word "निर्वन" means "complacency" or "satisfaction" and "सीधे" means "on" or "on top of". So the phrase "निर्वन के साथ" means "on complacency" or "on satisfaction".
The word "सँकल" means "sit" or "sitting", so the phrase "सँकल नहीं सकते" means "we cannot sit on our laurels".
In Hindi, we also use the word "हमें" which means "us" or "we", so the sentence "हमें निर्वन के साथ सीधे सँकल नहीं सकते" means "We cannot sit on our laurels".

I am giving you one sentence Translate this sentence from English to Hindi
Text: After all, why not?

Output:
Translated Hindi: क्या हमारे लिए नहीं था

Explanation:
In Hindi, the word "after" is translated as "क्या" (kya). The phrase "all" is translated as "हमारे" (hamare). The word "why" is translated as "क्या" (kya). And the word "not" is translated as "नहीं" (nahin).
